Definition and Categories of Divorce in Hanafi Fiqh
Defining divorce linguistically and legally, and listing its three categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and legal definitions of talaq and identify its three categories (ahsan, sunnah, bid'ah) according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Divorce (talaq) is the lifting of the marriage tie, and its best form is a single revocable pronouncement.

In this passage, the great Hanafi jurist al-Quduri (via al-Maydani's commentary) opens the Book of Divorce with a precise definition of talaq, distinguishing its linguistic root from its legal application. He then divides divorce into three categories, ranking them by compliance with the Sunnah. This lesson will help you parse these definitions and classifications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic definition
The text states that talaq linguistically means 'lifting a restriction' (رفع القيد), but it is used specifically for women as divorce.
2
Distinguish explicit from allusive expressions
The text notes the difference between 'mutallaqa' (with tashdid) as explicit, and 'mutilaqa' (with takhfif) as kinayah (allusion).
3
Extract the legal definition
The legal definition is 'lifting the marriage tie in the present or future with a specific expression.' Note the two dimensions of time (immediate vs. future) and the requirement of a specific expression.
4
List the three categories as given by the author
Ahsan (most beautiful): single revocable divorce (as in Zahir al-Riwayah). Talaq al-Sunnah (divorce according to the Sunnah): to be defined later. Talaq al-Bid'ah (innovative divorce). Note al-Karkhi's division into two only.
5
Focus on the first category
The text begins describing 'ahsan' as a single revocable divorce, citing it as the position of Zahir al-Riwayah.
The text cuts off here; refer to additional sources for full description.

Book of Divorce. Its suitability to fosterage is that each of them is prohibited. Lexically it is: lifting of a restriction, but they applied it to a woman as divorce, and to other things as release. Thus you say 'mutallaqa' with tashdid explicitly, and 'mutilaqa' with takhif as a kinayah. Legally: lifting the marriage tie in the present or in the future with a specific expression. [Divisions of Divorce:] And its divisions are three, as the author states: 'Divorce is of three types: the most beautiful divorce, the divorce of the Sunnah, and the divorce of innovation.' And al-Karkhi made it two: divorce of the Sunnah and divorce of innovation. [The Most Beautiful Divorce:] (The most beautiful divorce relative to its other divisions is that a man divorces his wife a single revocable divorce, as in the apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah) — and in 'Ziyadat...

Commentary
This passage opens the Book of Divorce with definitions and classifications. The passage type is a definition and categorization. The text first connects divorce with fosterage (both prohibited matters). Then it gives the linguistic definition of talaq as 'lifting a restriction', but notes that it is used specifically for a woman (divorce) and for other things as 'release'. It distinguishes between 'mutallaqa' (with tashdid) as explicit divorce and 'mutilaqa' (with takhif) as kinayah (allusive expression). The legal definition: lifting the marriage tie immediately or in the future with a specific expression. Then it lists the three categories: ahsan (most beautiful), sunnah (customary/approved), and bid'ah (innovation). It mentions that al-Karkhi categorizes it into two: sunnah and bid'ah. Finally, it begins explaining 'ahsan al-talaq' as a single revocable divorce, citing it as the Zahir al-Riwayah position and referencing 'Ziyadat'.

Key Terms
الطلاق (at-talaq): Divorce: lifting the marriage tie in the present or future with a specific expression
الطلاق الرجعي (at-talaq ar-raj'i): Revocable divorce – the husband can take back his wife during the iddah without a new marriage contract
أحسن الطلاق (ahsan at-talaq): The most beautiful divorce: a single revocable divorce
طلاق السنة (talaq as-sunnah): Divorce according to the Sunnah: divorcing a woman once during a tuhr (pure state) that she has not been touched in
طلاق البدعة (talaq al-bid'ah): Innovative divorce: divorcing during menstruation or in a tuhr that the husband has touched her

Key Takeaway
Divorce is legally defined as lifting the marriage tie with a specific expression, and the best form is a single revocable pronouncement.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Definition and Types of Divorce (Talaq)
Defines talaq and classifies its forms

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of talaq, distinguish between its linguistic and legal meanings, and correctly identify and explain the three types: ahsan, sunnah, and bid'ah.

Core Idea
Divorce removes the marriage bond; the best form is one revocable divorce in a state of purity.

The Book of Divorce opens with a precise definition of talaq, both in language and in law. Imam al-Quduri then classifies divorce into three categories, highlighting the prophetic ideal and warning against prohibited practices. This lesson will walk you through the definition and each type, clarifying what makes a divorce valid, recommended, or blameworthy.

Guided Path
1
Understand the linguistic vs. legal definition
Note that linguistically talaq means 'removing a restriction,' but legally it is the removal of the marriage bond immediately (ba'in) or eventually (raj'i) with a specific word. The linguistic usage extends to other things (itlaq), but in law it is confined to marriage.
The word 'talaq' is reserved for the wife; for a slave or other it is 'itlaq'.
2
Distinguish explicit and kinayah wording
The phrase 'anti mutallaqah' (with tashdid) is explicit (sareeh) and effects divorce without intention. 'Mutlaqah' (without tashdid) is kinayah (metaphorical) and requires intention.
This distinction is derived from the linguistic discussion.
3
Identify the three types and their features
The best divorce (ahsan) is one revocable divorce in a tuhr without intercourse, leaving her to complete iddah. Sunnah divorce is three divorces in three separate tuhrs. Bid'ah divorce is three or two divorces with one word.
Note the intra-madhhab difference: ahsan is raj'i per Zahir al-Riwayah, but some texts allow ba'in.
4
Recognize the ruling (hukm) for each type
Ahsan and sunnah are sunnah muakkadah (recommended). Bid'ah is makruh tahrimi (prohibited but effective). The best practice is to follow the sunnah method.
Bid'ah divorce is sinful but still counts as valid divorce.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق
وهو لغةً: رَفْعُ القيد، لكن جعلوه في المرأة: طلاقاً، وفي غيرها إطلاقاً، ولذا كان أنت مُطَلَّقة بالتشديد : صريحاً، ومُطلقة : بالتخفيف: كناية.
وشرعاً : رفع قيد النكاح في الحال، أو المآل، بلفظ مخصوص.
الطلاق على ثلاثة أوجه : أحسنُ الطلاق، وطلاق السنة، وطلاق البدعة .
فأحسن الطلاق أن يُطلق الرجل امرأته تطليقةً واحدةً رجعيةً، كما في ظاهر الرواية ـ وفي «زيادات الزيادات»: البائن، والرجعي سواء كذا في «التصحيح» ـ في طُهْرٍ واحدٍ لم يجامعها فيه، ويَتْركها حتى تنقضى عِدَّتُها ؛ لأنه أبعد من الندامة؛ لتمكنه من التدارك، وأقل ضرراً بالمرأة.
وطلاق السُّنَّة : أن يُطلق المدخول بها ثلاثاً، في ثلاثة أطهار، في كل طهر تطليقة. ثم قيل : الأولى أن يؤخر الإيقاع إلى آخر الطَّهر، احترازاً عن تطويل العدة، والأظهر أن يطلقها كما طهرت؛ لأنه لو أخر: ربما يجامعها، ومَنْ قَصده التطليق، فيُبتلى بالإيقاع عقيب الوقاع.
وطلاق البدعة : هو أن يطلقها ثلاثاً، أو اثنتين بكلمة واحدة.
Book of Divorce. It is linguistically: removal of the restriction, but they made it for the woman: 'talaq' (divorce), and for other things: 'itlaq' (release). Hence 'anti mutallaqah' (with tashdid) is explicit, and 'mutlaqah' (with takhfif) is metaphorical. Legally: removal of the marriage bond immediately or eventually, with a specific word. Divorce is of three types: the best divorce, sunnah divorce, and bid'ah divorce. The best divorce is that a man divorces his wife one revocable divorce, as in Zahir al-Riwayah—and in Ziyadat al-Ziyadat: the irrevocable and revocable are the same, as in al-Tashih—in one tuhr in which he did not have intercourse with her, and he leaves her until her iddah expires; because it is furthest from regret, enabling him to rectify, and least harmful to the woman. Sunnah divorce is that he divorces the one who was consummated with three divorces in three tuhrs, one divorce in each tuhr. Then it was said: it is better to postpone the pronouncement to the end of the tuhr, to avoid prolonging the iddah. But the more apparent is that he divorces her as soon as she becomes pure; because if he delays, perhaps he will have intercourse with her, and he intends divorce, so he may be afflicted with pronouncing divorce after intercourse. Bid'ah divorce is that he divorces her three, or two, with one word.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage from al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri opens the Book of Divorce. It provides both a linguistic and legal definition of talaq. Linguistically, talaq means 'removing a restriction,' but in legal usage it is specifically applied to the wife (talaq), while 'itlaq' is used for other things. This distinction explains why saying 'anti mutallaqah' (with tashdid) is an explicit divorce, while 'mutlaqah' (without tashdid) is a kinayah (metaphorical expression). The legal definition is the removal of the marriage bond immediately (ba'in divorce) or eventually (raj'i divorce) using a specific word. The passage then cites the author al-Quduri's classification of divorce into three types: ahsan (best), sunnah, and bid'ah. It notes that al-Karkhi divided it into only two types (sunnah and bid'ah), but the author follows the threefold division. The best divorce (ahsan) is one revocable divorce in a single tuhr (pure period) during which he did not have intercourse, then leaving her to complete her iddah. The wisdom is that it avoids regret and harms the woman least. The passage then clarifies a disagreement in the school: according to Zahir al-Riwayah the divorce is raj'i (revocable), but in Ziyadat al-Ziyadat both ba'in and raj'i are considered equal, meaning one can also be ba'in in this pattern. Sunnah divorce requires three divorces in three separate tuhrs for a consummated marriage. There is a discussion about timing: some say to delay until the end of the tuhr to avoid prolonging iddah, but the stronger view (al-azhar) is to pronounce divorce immediately upon purification to prevent intercourse, which could lead to pronouncing divorce after intercourse (which would be bid'ah). Finally, bid'ah divorce is defined as pronouncing three divorces (or two) in a single phrase, which is prohibited.

Key Terms
الطلاق (al-talaq): Legally: removal of the marriage bond immediately or eventually with a specific word.
أحسن الطلاق (ahsan al-talaq): One revocable divorce in a tuhr without intercourse, then leaving her until iddah ends.
طلاق السنة (talaq al-sunnah): Three divorces in three separate tuhrs for a consummated marriage.
طلاق البدعة (talaq al-bid'ah): Pronouncing three divorces (or two) with one word.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the most recommended form of divorce?
A) Three divorces in one sitting
B) One revocable divorce in a tuhr without intercourse
C) Two divorces in one menstrual period
D) Divorce pronounced during menstruation

Key Takeaway
The best divorce (ahsan) is one revocable pronouncement in a tuhr without intercourse, allowing reconciliation.

Sunnah and Bid'ah Divorce: Definitions and Rulings
Defines sunnah and bid'ah divorce with rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define sunnah and bid'ah divorce according to the Hanafi school and state the ruling for each.

Core Idea
Sunnah divorce is one divorce in a purity; bid'ah is three at once—both valid, but bid'ah is sinful.

This passage from a Hanafi commentary on al-Quduri distinguishes between sunnah (prophetic practice) and bid'ah (innovation) in divorce. Understanding this distinction is crucial: a divorce may be valid yet sinful, and the method prescribed by the Sunnah avoids sin. The text also clarifies the conditions for a sunnah divorce, specifically for a consummated wife.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definitions
Locate the definitions of talaq al-sunnah and talaq al-bid'ah in the passage. For sunnah: three divorces over three purities (or one divorce in a purity). For bid'ah: three divorces in one utterance or within one purity.
Note that the sunnah method is further split into timing and number.
2
Recognise the condition for sunnah divorce
The passage specifies that sunnah divorce applies to a consummated wife (al-madkhul biha) and must occur in a state of purity (tuhr) without intercourse in that purity.
A non-consummated wife can be divorced anytime; the sunnah conditions do not apply.
3
Understand the ruling for bid'ah divorce
The text states that if a husband divorces three times in a bid'ah manner, the divorce falls (is valid), the wife becomes irrevocably separated (ba'in), but the husband is sinful (asi).
The sin is for violating the sunnah method, not for the act of divorce itself.
4
Distinguish sunnah in timing vs. number
The passage concludes by separating the two aspects: sunnah in timing means she is pure; sunnah in number means one divorce (not three).
Thus the ideal sunnah divorce is a single pronouncement in a tuhr without intercourse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وطلاقُ السُّنَّةِ : أن يُطلِّقَ المُدخولَ بها ثلاثاً، في ثلاثة أطهارٍ . وطلاقُ البدعةِ : هو أن يُطلِّقَها ثلاثاً بكلمةٍ واحدةٍ، أو ثلاثاً في طُهْرٍ واحدٍ. فإذا فَعَلَ ذلك : وَقَعَ الطلاقُ، وبانت امرأتُهُ منه، وكان عاصياً. والسُّنَّةُ في الطلاقِ من وجهينِ : سُنَّةٌ في الوقتِ، وسنةٌ في العددِ. سُنَّةٌ في الوقتِ : بأن تكونَ طاهرةً، وسنةٌ في العددِ : بأن تكونَ واحدةً.
And sunnah divorce is that he divorces the one who has been consummated with three times in three purities. And bid'ah divorce is that he divorces her three times with one word, or three times in one purity. So if he does that, the divorce falls, and his wife becomes irrevocably separated from him, and he is sinful. And the sunnah in divorce is from two aspects: sunnah in timing and sunnah in number. Sunnah in timing: that she be in a state of purity; and sunnah in number: that it be one.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a ruling and definition statement from a Hanafi fiqh commentary. It defines two types of divorce: sunnah (commendable) and bid'ah (innovative). Sunnah divorce is to give three divorces over three separate purification periods (tuhrs) to a wife with whom intercourse has occurred. This allows for possible reconciliation. Bid'ah divorce is to give three divorces at once, either in one utterance or within a single purification period. The text then states the ruling: if a husband performs bid'ah divorce, the divorce is effective (the wife becomes irrevocably separated), but the husband commits a sin because he violated the recommended practice. Finally, it clarifies that the sunnah method has two dimensions: timing (when the wife is pure from menstruation and no intercourse has occurred in that purity) and number (only one divorce, not three).

Key Terms
طلاق السنة (talaq al-sunnah): Divorce that follows the prophetic practice: one divorce in a purity without intercourse, or three over three purities for a consummated wife.
طلاق البدعة (talaq al-bid'ah): Divorce that violates sunnah: usually three divorces at once or within one purity.
طهر (tuhr): The period of purity between two menstruations, during which the wife is not menstruating.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The divorce takes effect but only counts as one divorce.
D) The divorce is invalid unless the wife consents.

Key Takeaway
Sunnah divorce is one divorce in purity; bid'ah is three at once—valid but sinful.

Bid'ah Divorce: Valid Yet Sinful
Explanation of bid'ah divorce and its legal effect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bid'ah divorce, identify its evidence from the hadith of Ibn Umar, and explain the distinction between the validity of the pronouncement and the prohibition of its manner.

Core Idea
Bid'ah divorce counts legally, but the one who performs it is sinful for violating the Sunnah.

One of the most misunderstood rulings in Hanafi fiqh is that of bid'ah divorce. Many assume that a sinful act cannot be legally effective, yet the Hanafi school, drawing on the Prophet's ﷺ interaction with Ibn Umar, clearly distinguishes between the validity of the pronouncement and the prohibition of its manner. This lesson unpacks that distinction, the proof behind it, and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is bid'ah divorce? It is divorcing three times in one tuhr or during menstruation. According to the passage, the ruling is that the divorce occurs (waqa'a al-ṭalāq), the wife becomes separated, and the husband is disobedient (ʿāṣī). Thus, the act is valid but sinful.
The passage explicitly states: فإذا فَعَلَ ذلك : وَقَعَ الطلاق، وبانت امراته منه، وكان عاصياً.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar, where he divorced his wife bid'ah, and the Prophet ﷺ ordered him to take her back. This indicates that the divorce was effective—otherwise there would be no need for taking her back. The footnote references Sahih al-Bukhari and Nasb al-Rayah.
The Prophet's order to take her back (مراجعة) implies the divorce counted; it was not nullified by its bid'ah nature.
3
Understand the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
The passage explains that the default ruling for divorce is prohibition (al-ḥaẓr) because it cuts off marriage with its religious and worldly benefits. Divorce is permitted only out of necessity for release. Since a single divorce satisfies that need, adding more is wasteful extravagance (isrāf) and thus becomes bid'ah.
The reasoning connects the sinfulness to excess, not to the essence of the divorce.
4
Distinguish between validity and sinfulness
The prohibition attaches to the manner (kayfiyya) of divorce, not to the substance (dhāt) of the pronouncement. Hence the pronouncement remains legally effective, but the manner is forbidden (makrūh taḥrīmī). This is a key principle: a valid act can be sinful if prohibited due to an external factor.
This distinction is essential for correctly applying Hanafi rulings on talaq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحدة، أو ثلاثاً في طُهْرٍ واحد.
فإذا فَعَلَ ذلك : وَقَعَ الطلاق، وبانت امراته منه، وكان عاصياً. والسُّنَّةُ في الطلاق من وجهين : سُنَّةٌ في الوقت، وسنةٌ في العدد.
واحدة، أو يطلقها (ثلاثاً)، أو اثنتين (في طهر واحد)؛ لأن الأصل في الطلاق الحظر؛ لما فيه من قطع النكاح الذي تعلقت به المصالح الدينية والدنيوية، والإباحة إنما هي للحاجة إلى الخلاص، ولا حاجة إلى الجمع بين الثلاث، أو في طَهْرٍ واحد، لأن الحاجة تندفع بالواحدة، وتمامُ الخَلاص فى المفرَّق على الأطهار، فالزيادة إسراف؛ فكان بدعة.
(1) أي طلاق البدعة.
(٢) أي النهي عن طلاق البدعة ينظر صحيح البخاري ٣٤٥/٩ (٥٢٥١)، ونصب الراية ،۲۲۰۳ ، وفيهما طلاق ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما امرأته طلاق بدعة، وأمر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم له بمراجعتها، وفي بعض الروايات عند الدارقطني وغيره: یابن عمر ! ما هكذا أَمَرَك الله ، قد أخطأت السنة».
One, or three in one period of purity. So when he does that: the divorce occurs, and his wife becomes irrevocably separated from him, and he is disobedient. And the Sunnah in divorce is in two respects: Sunnah in time, and Sunnah in number. One, or he divorces her (three) or two (in one tuhr); because the original ruling regarding divorce is prohibition; due to what it involves of cutting off marriage which is linked to religious and worldly interests, and permissibility is only due to the need for release, and there is no need to combine three, or in one tuhr, because need is satisfied with one, and complete release is in separation over several tuhrs, so the increase is extravagance; thus it is innovation. (1) i.e., bid'ah divorce. (2) i.e., the prohibition of bid'ah divorce; see Sahih al-Bukhari 9/345 (5251), and Nasb al-Rayah 2/203, in both of which is the story of Ibn Umar divorcing his wife bid'ah, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered him to take her back, and in some narrations by al-Daraqutni and others: 'O Ibn Umar! This is not what Allah commanded you; you have violated the Sunnah.'
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage states that bid'ah divorce—such as giving three divorces in one clean period—is sinful but legally effective. The author explains that the default ruling of divorce is prohibition (ʿadam al-ibāḥa) because it dissolves marriage, which has many benefits. Divorce is only permitted out of necessity for release. Since a single divorce suffices for that need, giving three at once is wasteful and thus bid'ah. The footnote references the hadith of Ibn ʿUmar, where the Prophet ﷺ ordered him to take back his wife after a bid'ah divorce, confirming that the divorce still counts. This shows that the prohibition is due to an external factor (the manner) and does not strip the act of its legal effect (the pronouncement is valid).

Key Terms
طلاق البدعة (ṭalāq al-bidʿah): A divorce that violates the sunnah in timing or number, e.g., divorcing three times in one tuhr or during menstruation.
السنة في الطلاق (al-sunnah fī al-ṭalāq): The recommended way to divorce: once during a clean period without intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Only one divorce counts, and the other two are disregarded.
D) The divorce is valid only if the wife is not menstruating at the time.

Key Takeaway
Bid'ah divorce is legally effective but sinful; the prohibition attaches to its manner, not its validity.

Sunnah Divorce: Conditions and Application
Ruling on bid'ah divorce validity and sunnah divorce conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between sunnah and bid'ah divorce, state the two sunnah conditions (time and number), and apply them to consummated and non-consummated wives.

Core Idea
Sunnah divorce requires one pronouncement in a clean period without intercourse; violating this is sinful but the divorce still counts.

This passage explains the two aspects of sunnah divorce: timing and number. It also clarifies that a divorce given in a prohibited manner (bid'ah) is still valid, though sinful. Understanding these distinctions is essential for correctly applying the Hanafi rules on talaq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two aspects
Recognize that sunnah divorce has two components: sunnah in time (al-sunnah fī al-waqt) and sunnah in number (al-sunnah fī al-‘adad).
These are mentioned explicitly in the text.
2
Distinguish the application of each aspect
Sunnah in number (one divorce) applies to all wives regardless of consummation. Sunnah in time (divorce during a tuhr without intercourse) applies only to the consummated wife.
For non-consummated, time is irrelevant because she has no iddah.
3
Analyze the ruling on bid'ah divorce
The text states that if a husband performs a bid'ah divorce (e.g., during menstruation), the divorce still occurs and counts, but he is disobedient (asi). The reason is that the prohibition is due to an external factor (li ma'nan fī ghayrihi), so the act retains its legal validity.
This is a key Hanafi principle: prohibitions attached to external factors do not nullify the act.
4
Apply to a non-consummated wife scenario
For a wife who has not been consummated, the sunnah in time does not apply. The husband may divorce her in purity or menstruation; both are sunnah because she has no waiting period to be harmed.
The text says: 'وغير المدخول بها أن يطلقها في حال الطهر والحيض جميعاً'.
5
Consider the missing continuation
The passage begins to discuss a woman who does not menstruate (e.g., due to age), but the text is cut off. Note that this scenario is treated separately in later passages.
OCR risk: incomplete text.

Sunnah Divorce: Number and Timing
Defines sunnah divorce in number and timing for both types of women

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two aspects of sunnah divorce (number and timing) and distinguish between consummated and non-consummated women in the application of timing.

Core Idea
Sunnah divorce: one pronouncement in a pure state without intercourse for consummated women; any time for non-consummated.

This passage from Al-Lubab clarifies the sunnah method of divorce. The ruling is divided into two dimensions: the number of pronouncements and the timing. While the number requirement (one divorce per period) applies to both consummated and non-consummated women, the timing restriction applies only to those who were consummated. Understanding this distinction prevents common misconceptions about when a divorce follows the sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two dimensions of sunnah divorce
Recognize that the passage divides sunnah divorce into two separate rulings: the number of pronouncements (al-ʿadad) and the timing (al-waqt).
These are independent conditions; each has its own applicability.
2
Analyze the ruling on number
Note that the sunnah in number is the same for both consummated and non-consummated women: one pronouncement per period of purity. The prohibition of triple divorce in one utterance applies to all women due to the risk of regret.
This is a universal sunnah rule.
3
Analyze the ruling on timing for consummated women
For a consummated woman, the sunnah timing requires that the husband divorces her once during a state of purity (tuhr) in which he has not had intercourse with her. The rationale is that divorce should occur at a time when desire may renew, avoiding periods of aversion (menstruation) or times when desire has subsided (after intercourse).
If he divorces during menstruation or in a tuhr with intercourse, it is bid'ah.
4
Analyze the ruling on timing for non-consummated women
For a non-consummated woman, there is no timing restriction; she may be divorced in purity or menstruation. The reason is that she has no waiting period (ʿiddah), and her desire is constant, so waiting would cause harm without benefit.
This is because the rationale (desire) is present in all states.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق
فالسنَّة فى العدد يستوي فيها المدخول بها، وغير المدخول بها؛ لأن الطلاق الثلاث في كلمة واحدة، إنما منع منه خوفاً من الندم، وهو موجود في غير المدخول بها.
والسنة في الوقت، تثبت في حق المدخول بها خاصة، وهو: أن يطلقها واحدةً في طُهْرٍ لم يجامعها فيه، لأن المراعي دليلُ الحاجة، وهو الإقدام على الطلاق في زمان تجدد الرغبة، وهو الخالي عن الجماع، أما زمانُ الحيض فزمان النُّفْرة، وبالجماع مرةً في الطهر : تفتر الرغبة.
وغير المدخول بها أن يطلقها في حال الطهر والحيض جميعاً؛ لأن الرغبة بها صادقة في كل حال، ولا عدة عليها، فتتضرر بطولها.
Book of Divorce. The sunnah in number is the same for the consummated woman and the non-consummated woman, because triple divorce in one utterance is prohibited only out of fear of regret, and that exists in the non-consummated woman. The sunnah in timing is established only in the case of the consummated woman, and it is: that he divorces her once in a state of purity in which he has not had intercourse with her, because what is considered is the evidence of need, which is proceeding with divorce at a time of renewed desire, and that is the time free from intercourse. As for the time of menstruation, it is a time of aversion, and by having intercourse once in the state of purity, desire subsides. As for the non-consummated woman, he may divorce her in both the state of purity and menstruation, because her desire is honest in every situation, and she has no waiting period, so she would be harmed by its prolongation.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage explains the two aspects of sunnah divorce (talaq al-sunnah): number and timing. In terms of number, the sunnah method is to divorce with one pronouncement per period of purity, and this applies equally whether the woman has been consummated or not. Triple divorce in one utterance is prohibited because it may lead to regret, and this risk exists for all women. In terms of timing, the sunnah applies only to women who have been consummated: the husband should divorce her once during a state of purity (tuhr) in which he has not had intercourse with her. The rationale is that divorce should happen at a time when desire may renew, which is after menstruation but before intercourse—intercourse reduces desire. For a non-consummated woman, there is no waiting period (iddah), and she experiences consistent desire, so she may be divorced in either purity or menstruation without harm.

Key Terms
طلاق السنة (talaq al-sunnah): The method of divorce that follows the sunnah: one pronouncement per period of purity, with specific timing.
مدخول بها (madkhul biha): A woman with whom the husband has consummated the marriage.
غير مدخول بها (ghayr madkhul biha): A woman with whom the husband has not consummated the marriage.
طهر (tuhr): State of purity from menstruation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The sunnah for consummated women requires one divorce in a purity without intercourse; for non-consummated women timing is unrestricted.

Sunnah Divorce for Non-Menstruating Woman and Month Calculation
Ruling and intra-madhhab dispute on month calculation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure for sunnah divorce of a non-menstruating woman and calculate the months under the views of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A month replaces the menstrual cycle for a non-menstruating woman, but the calculation method differs among the Hanafi imams.

Divorcing according to the sunnah requires proper spacing between pronouncements. For a woman who does not menstruate, the month takes the place of the menstrual cycle. However, how to count those months—especially when the divorce occurs mid-month—is disputed within the Hanafi school. This lesson unpacks the procedure and the intra-madhhab difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its legal category
Determine what the passage rules: it prescribes the sunnah method (sunnah muakkadah) for divorcing a non-menstruating woman. Note that the month stands in the place of the menstrual period.
This is a recommended method, not obligatory.
2
Trace the analogy (qiyas) behind the ruling
The passage says 'because the month in her case stands in place of menstruation'. Identify the asl (menstruating woman) and the illa (need for a temporal measure).
The qiyas is from the menstrual cycle to the month as a time marker.
3
Distinguish the two calculation methods
Compare Abu Hanifa's rule (lunar months if at start, 30-day months if mid-month) with the Sahibayn's rule (first month completed by the last, middle months by lunar months).
Apply this to both the spacing between divorces and the iddah.
4
Apply to a concrete scenario
Take a hypothetical: a man divorces his elderly wife on the 15th of Muharram. Calculate the next divorce dates under both methods.
Note the practical difference in total days.
5
Relate to other fiqh issues
The passage mentions مسألة الإجارات (lease contracts). See how the same dispute applies there.
Consistency of usul across chapters.

وإذا كانت المرأة ممن لا تحيض من صِغَرٍ أو كبر، فأراد أن يطلقها للسنة : طلقها واحدةً وتركها حتى يمضي شهر، فإذا مضى شهر: طلقها طلقة أخرى، وتركها أيضاً حتى يمضي شهر آخر، فإذا مضى شهر آخر : طلقها طلقة أخرى، فتصير ثلاث طلقات في ثلاثة أشهر ; لأن الشهر في حقها قائم مقام الحيض. ثم إن كان الطلاق في أول الشهر : تُعتبر الشهور بالأهلة، وإن كان في وسطه : فبالأيام في حق التفريق. وفي حق العدة : كذلك عند أبي حنيفة " وعندهما: يُكَمَّلُ الأولُ بالأخير والمتوسطان بالأهلة، وهي مسألة الإجارات.
If the woman does not menstruate due to young age or old age, and he wishes to divorce her according to the sunnah: he divorces her once and leaves her until a month passes, then when a month passes, he divorces her another divorce, and leaves her again until another month passes, then when another month passes, he divorces her another divorce, so she becomes three divorces in three months, because the month in her case stands in the place of menstruation. Then, if the divorce occurs at the beginning of the month, the months are calculated by lunar months, and if it occurs in the middle, then by days in terms of the interval. And in terms of the waiting period, it is the same according to Abu Hanifah. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the first month is completed by the last, and the middle months by lunar months, and this is the issue of leases.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage details the procedure for a woman who does not menstruate (e.g., a young girl or an old woman past menopause). Since she has no menstrual cycles, a month takes the place of the menstrual period for spacing divorces. The husband divorces her once each month for three months, resulting in three divorces. The calculation of the months depends on timing: if he divorces at the beginning of a month, months are counted by lunar months (hilal); if in the middle, by thirty-day months. For the waiting period (iddah), Imam Abu Hanifah applies the same rule. However, his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, differ: they hold that the first incomplete month is completed by the last month (adding days to make it a full month), and the middle months are counted by lunar months. This same disagreement appears in the issue of leasing (ijarah) for a period of months.

Key Terms
شهر (shahr): A month used to measure the interval between divorces for a non-menstruating woman.
أهلة (ahillah): Lunar months calculated by sighting the crescent.
عدة (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce before remarrying.
مسألة الإجارات (mas'alat al-ijarat): The issue of leasing for known months, where a similar dispute exists about calculation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) By lunar months (crescent sightings).
B) By 30-day months.
C) The first month is completed by the last, middle months by lunar months.
D) The month is not counted.

Key Takeaway
For sunnah divorce of a non-menstruating woman, space divorces one month apart; if the first divorce is mid-month, count each month as 30 days under the mufta bihi view.

The Sunnah Method of Divorce
Explains the recommended method of divorcing with monthly intervals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the sunnah method of divorce and state the rule for counting months when divorce occurs at the beginning or middle of a month.

Core Idea
For sunnah divorce, one divorce per month; months counted by lunar months if at beginning, by days if in middle.

Divorce is a serious matter, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) prescribed a specific method to ensure fairness and deliberation. This lesson explains the recommended (sunnah) method of divorcing one's wife by spacing three divorces over three months, and how to count the months when the divorce occurs at the beginning or middle of a month.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being described and its legal classification. Here, it is the sunnah method of divorce, which is recommended (sunnah muakkadah).
The passage begins by stating 'He divorces her according to the Sunnah'.
2
Understand the process of sunnah divorce
The husband pronounces one divorce, then waits a month, pronounces a second, waits another month, and pronounces a third – thus three divorces in three months.
The month takes the place of menstruation for non-menstruating women.
3
Apply the rule for counting months
If the divorce is pronounced at the beginning of a month, count by lunar months (based on the crescent). If in the middle, count by days (30 days per month).
This rule applies to the separation (tafriq) of divorces.
4
Recognize the analogy to menstruation
The month stands in place of the menstrual cycle (tuhr) for the purpose of spacing divorces.
This analogy is the basis for using months.

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Divorce explains the Sunnah method of divorce (al-talāq al-sunnī). The opening clarifies that a husband should pronounce a single divorce after each menstrual period (or month for non-menstruating women) over three months, thus completing three divorces. The rationale is that a month stands in place of menstruation for determining the 'idda. The commentary then addresses a fiqh nuance: if the divorce is pronounced at the beginning of a month, months are counted by the lunar calendar; if in the middle, days are used for the purpose of separating divorces. A disagreement arises between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, regarding the calculation for the 'idda. According to Abu Hanifa, the same rule applies (start with lunar months, middle with days). According to the Sahibayn, the first incomplete month is completed with the last, and the middle months are counted by lunar months. This is analogous to the issue of lease contracts (ijārāt), where similar differences exist. The footnote clarifies that a narration from Abu Yusuf supports Abu Hanifa's view, but the relied-upon position in the madhhab is as stated.

Key Terms
السنة (al-sunnah): The recommended method of divorce as practiced by the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم), involving one divorce per menstrual cycle (or month) over three cycles.
تفريق الطلاق (tafriq al-talaq): Spreading the three divorces over separate months, as opposed to pronouncing them all at once.
مسألة الإجارات (mas'alat al-ijārāt): The legal issue of lease contracts when the term is a month or year starting mid-month; analogy is made to divorce 'idda calculation.

Key Takeaway
The sunnah method of divorce requires one divorce per month, with months counted by lunar months if at the beginning, or by 30-day periods if in the middle.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on 'Iddah Month Calculation
Discusses the intra-Hanafi dispute on month calculation for 'iddah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding 'iddah calculation when divorce occurs mid-month, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
When divorce occurs mid-month, Abu Hanifa counts 'iddah by days; the Sahibayn complete the first with the last month.

In the previous lesson we learned the recommended method of divorcing. However, a subtle disagreement arises among Hanafi imams regarding how to calculate the 'iddah (waiting period) when the divorce is pronounced in the middle of a lunar month. This lesson unpacks this intra-madhhab dispute and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The dispute centres on how to calculate the 'iddah of three months when the divorce occurs in the middle of a lunar month: should one count by days or by a combination of lunar months and days?
The same issue arises for the separation of divorces, but the text here specifically discusses 'iddah.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the rule for 'iddah is the same as for the separation: if divorce at beginning, count by lunar months; if in middle, count by days (30 days per month).
Thus the 'iddah ends exactly 90 days from the divorce date.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the first incomplete month is completed with the last month (by adding days), and the middle months are counted by lunar months.
For example, if divorce on 15th Muharram, the first month runs from 15th Muharram to end of Muharram (say 30 days? Actually they complete the first month with days from the last month, and the middle months are full lunar months.
4
Understand the analogy with lease contracts
The same disagreement appears in lease contracts (ijarat): if a lease begins mid-month, Abu Hanifa counts the year as 360 days; the Sahibayn complete the first with the last month and count intermediate months by lunar months.
This shows the principle is applied consistently across different areas of fiqh.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text notes that a narration from Abu Yusuf supports Abu Hanifa, and some authorities state the fatwa is on the opinion of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) because it is easier.
The mufta bihi is thus the view that counts 'iddah by days (90 days) when divorce occurs in mid-month.

Book of Divorce. He divorces her according to the Sunnah: he divorces her once and leaves her until a month passes, then when a month passes he divorces her with another divorce, and leaves her again until another month passes, then when another month passes he divorces her with another divorce, so she becomes three divorces in three months; because the month for her takes the place of menstruation. * Then if the divorce was at the beginning of the month, the months are counted by lunar months, and if it was in the middle, then by days regarding the separation. (2) And regarding the waiting period ('idda), it is the same according to Abu Hanifa. And according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the first [month] is completed with the last (3), and the middle [months] are by lunar months (4), and this is the issue of leases (5). (1) i.e., in spreading the divorce over the months, each month is counted as thirty days regarding the pronouncing of divorce. Al-Binaya 14/5. (2) And it is a narration from Abu Yusuf as well. Fath al-Qadir 3/335. (3) i.e., the first month is completed with the last month by days. (4) Because the origin for the month is lunar months. (5) And it is: if one leases known months or a year during the middle of a month, the disagreement between the Imam (Abu Hanifa) and the two companions is like the disagreement here: according to the Imam, the year is 360 days, and according to the two, the first is completed with the last, and what is between is considered by lunar months. Al-Binaya 14/5.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Divorce explains the Sunnah method of divorce (al-talāq al-sunnī). The opening clarifies that a husband should pronounce a single divorce after each menstrual period (or month for non-menstruating women) over three months, thus completing three divorces. The rationale is that a month stands in place of menstruation for determining the 'idda. The commentary then addresses a fiqh nuance: if the divorce is pronounced at the beginning of a month, months are counted by the lunar calendar; if in the middle, days are used for the purpose of separating divorces. A disagreement arises between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, regarding the calculation for the 'idda. According to Abu Hanifa, the same rule applies (start with lunar months, middle with days). According to the Sahibayn, the first incomplete month is completed with the last, and the middle months are counted by lunar months. This is analogous to the issue of lease contracts (ijārāt), where similar differences exist. The footnote clarifies that a narration from Abu Yusuf supports Abu Hanifa's view, but the relied-upon position in the madhhab is as stated.

Key Terms
السنة (al-sunnah): The recommended method of divorce as practiced by the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم), involving one divorce per menstrual cycle (or month) over three cycles.
تفريق الطلاق (tafriq al-talaq): Spreading the three divorces over separate months, as opposed to pronouncing them all at once.
مسألة الإجارات (mas'alat al-ijārāt): The legal issue of lease contracts when the term is a month or year starting mid-month; analogy is made to divorce 'idda calculation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon) view in the Hanafi school, if a woman is divorced in the middle of a month, how is her 'iddah calculated?
A) Three lunar months from the date of divorce
B) 90 days from the date of divorce
C) The first month completed with the last, middle months by lunar months
D) Only two lunar months plus days

Key Takeaway
When divorce occurs in the middle of a month, the relied-upon Hanafi view counts 'iddah by days (90 days), not by lunar months.

Divorcing a Non-Menstruating Woman After Intercourse: The Ruling and Its Cause
States the permissibility of immediate divorce for a non-menstruating woman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for divorcing a non-menstruating woman immediately after intercourse and explain the 'illa that makes it permissible.

Core Idea
Divorcing a non-menstruating woman after intercourse is permissible because the 'illa of doubt over pregnancy is absent.

This passage from Al-Lubab clarifies an important exception in the law of divorce. While divorcing a menstruating woman during her period is disliked due to uncertainty about pregnancy, the same concern does not apply to women who do not menstruate. Understanding this ruling sharpens your ability to identify the effective cause ('illa) in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general ruling
The act is divorcing a woman immediately after intercourse. The general rule for menstruating women is that it is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) to do so without an interval.
The base ruling comes from the avoidance of uncertainty about the start of 'idda.
2
Recognize the exception: the non-menstruating woman
The passage states that a woman who does not menstruate—either due to young age (before menarche) or old age (post-menopause)—may be divorced immediately after intercourse without any separation in time.
Her condition is key: la taḥīḍ.
3
Extract the 'illa (effective cause)
The prohibition for menstruating women is due to 'tawahhum al-ḥabal' (suspicion of pregnancy). This is the 'illa that triggers the dislike.
The 'illa is explicitly mentioned in the commentary: 'because the dislike is for one who menstruates due to the suspicion of pregnancy.'
4
Apply the absence of 'illa to derive the ruling
Since a non-menstruating woman cannot be suspected of pregnancy (or pregnancy is impossible), the 'illa is absent. Therefore, the reason for the prohibition vanishes, and the divorce becomes permissible (mubah) without any interval.
This is a straightforward rational proof (dalīl 'aqlī) based on the presence or absence of the cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز أن يطلقها ولا يفصل بين وطئها وطلاقها بزمان . ويجوز أن يطلقها أي مَنْ لا تحيض، ولا يفصل بين وطئها، وطلاقها بزمان؛ لأن الكراهية فيمن تحيض لتوهم الحبل، وهو مفقود هنا.
And it is permissible to divorce her and not separate between intercourse and divorce by any time. And it is permissible to divorce her, meaning she who does not menstruate, and not separate between intercourse and divorce by any time; because the dislike is for one who menstruates due to the suspicion of pregnancy, and that is absent here.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This short passage addresses the ruling for divorcing a woman who does not menstruate, such as a young girl (before menarche) or an old woman (post-menopause). The matn states that it is permissible to divorce her immediately after intercourse without any waiting period. The commentary explains the rationale: the prohibition (karāha) of divorcing a menstruating woman during her menses is due to the possibility of pregnancy being unknown. Since for a non-menstruating woman pregnancy is either impossible or clearly absent, that concern does not exist, so the divorce is permissible without interval. This is a clear ruling based on the underlying cause ('illa): the avoidance of doubt about the start of the 'idda.

Key Terms
لا تحيض (lā taḥīḍ): A woman who does not menstruate, either due to young age (before menarche) or old age (post-menopause).
توهم الحبل (tawahhum al-ḥabal): Suspicion or possibility of pregnancy, which is the reason for the prohibition of divorce during menses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because she cannot become pregnant.
B) Because there is no concern about confusion regarding the start of the 'idda.
C) Because the husband has the right to divorce anytime.
D) Because the Sunnah allows it for all women.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of divorcing a non-menstruating woman after intercourse is based on the absence of the 'illa that makes such a divorce disliked for menstruating women.

Divorce of a Pregnant Woman: Number of Divorces in Sunnah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sunnah divorce count for pregnant woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the number of divorces for a pregnant woman and identify the mufta bihi (operative) ruling with its evidence.

Core Idea
For a pregnant woman, the Sunnah method of divorce: three divorces (Abu Hanifa) vs. one divorce (Muhammad) — the mufta bihi is one.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the recommended (sunnah) number of pronouncements when divorcing a pregnant woman. While Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf compare her to a non-menstruating woman and permit three monthly divorces, Imam Muhammad and Zufar argue that since her 'idda ends with delivery, only one divorce is necessary. The prevailing fatwa follows Muhammad's view, making it the operative practice.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Unique Position of the Pregnant Woman
Recognize that divorce of a pregnant woman is permissible immediately after intercourse because pregnancy makes the 'idda clear (she delivers the baby), unlike a menstruating woman where confusion may arise. This sets the context for the dispute.
The permissibility is not disputed; only the Sunnah number is.
2
State the Two Competing Views
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that three divorces, each separated by a month, are Sunnah. Muhammad and Zufar hold that only one divorce is Sunnah.
Remember that the dispute is within the Hanafi school itself.
3
Examine the Rationale (Dalil Aqli) for Each View
For Abu Hanifa: analogy to the non-pregnant woman (who menstruates or is postmenopausal) — the month spacing allows for reconciliation. For Muhammad: the original principle that the 'idda of a pregnant woman ends with delivery, so prolonging divorces is unnecessary and contradicts the purpose of ease.
Both are reasoning-based (dalil aqli); no explicit textual proof is cited.
4
Identify the Mufta Bihi and Its Authority
The footnote from Fath al-Qadir (quoted by Ibn Abidin) states that the fatwa on the view of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is not strong. The relied-upon position is Muhammad's (single divorce).
This tarjih is based on later Hanafi masters, not on the strength of the proofs.

Commentary
This passage discusses the divorce of a pregnant woman. The matn states that it is permissible to divorce her immediately after sexual intercourse, unlike a menstruating woman. The commentary explains that this is because pregnancy makes the 'idda clear (she delivers the baby), so there is no confusion. Also, during pregnancy, there is a desire for intercourse, so prohibiting divorce would lead to hardship. Then a dispute arises regarding the recommended (sunnah) number of divorces. According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, it is sunnah to pronounce three divorces over three months, similar to a non-pregnant woman of childbearing age or a young girl. However, Imam Muhammad and Zufar hold that only one divorce is sunnah for a pregnant woman, and anything more would be bid'ah. The original principle is that the 'idda of a pregnant woman ends with delivery, so prolonging divorces is unnecessary. The footnote from Fath al-Qadir notes that while some say the fatwa is on the opinion of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), this is not strong (laysa bishay'in). The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school today is the opinion of Muhammad, that a pregnant woman is divorced only once in the sunnah method.

Key Terms
الحامل (al-ḥāmil): A pregnant woman whose pregnancy is known and can be used to determine the 'idda (ends with delivery).
السنة (al-sunnah): The recommended method of divorce, which for a pregnant woman is disputed whether one or three divorces; the fuqaha differ.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Three divorces, one per month.
B) Two divorces.
C) One divorce only.
D) No divorce is allowed until delivery.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that a pregnant woman should be divorced only once in the Sunnah method, due to her 'idda ending with delivery.

Sunna Divorce of a Pregnant Woman: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sunna divorce count for a pregnant woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sunna divorce of a pregnant woman, explain the reasoning of each side, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Does sunna divorce for a pregnant woman require three monthly divorces or just one? The Hanafi school splits.

This lesson examines a nuanced dispute within the Hanafi school: how many divorces should a husband pronounce to his pregnant wife in accordance with the sunna? The disagreement hinges on whether the month is a valid interval for a pregnant woman whose 'iddah ends with childbirth. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to trace how analogy and default principles operate within the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the exact point of disagreement: the number of divorces for a pregnant woman divorced according to sunna.
2
Present the first view
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: three divorces separated by a month. Understand their dalil: analogy to post-menopausal (ayisa) and minor (saghira) women, where the month indicates need.
Their reasoning: permission is due to need (hajah), and the month is an indicator of that need.
3
Present the opposing view
State the position of Muhammad and Zufar: only one divorce. Understand their dalil: the default (asl) is prohibition, and the law separates divorces based on intervals of the waiting period. Since a month is not an interval for a pregnant woman (her 'iddah ends with delivery), she is like a woman with extended purity.
They argue the pregnant woman is analogous to a woman whose period of purity is indefinitely extended, for whom only one divorce per cycle is permissible.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Explain how Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf respond: the month remains a valid practical interval even for pregnant women, preserving the sunna's purpose of allowing reflection and preventing hasty divorce.
The qiyas is based on the 'illa of need (hajah), which is common to all women regardless of waiting period type.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Identify the relied-upon position: the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as adopted by later authorities like al-Mahbubi, al-Nasafi, and al-Mawsili.
The tarjih is based on the strength of the analogy and the practical utility of the month as a spacing mechanism.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage discusses the sunna method for divorcing a pregnant woman. The matn states that it is permissible to divorce a pregnant woman immediately after intercourse, and the sunna method is to pronounce three divorces separated by a month, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Imam Muhammad says only one divorce is sunna. The sharh explains their reasoning: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf analogize to the case of post-menopausal and minor women, where the sunna is also three divorces with monthly intervals, due to the need (hajah) and the month as an indicator of the waiting period. Muhammad and Zufar argue that the default is prohibition, and that the law has established separation based on the intervals of the waiting period; for a pregnant woman, the waiting period ends with childbirth, not months, so a month is not a valid interval, making the pregnant woman like one with an extended period of purity (who should only be divorced once per cycle). The mufta bihi position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as adopted by later authorities.

Key Terms
الحامل (al-hamil): A pregnant woman whose 'iddah ends with delivery.
السنة (al-sunnah): The recommended method of pronouncing divorce following the practice of the Prophet.
الآيسة (al-ayisa): A post-menopausal woman who no longer menstruates.
الصغيرة (al-saghirah): A minor girl who has not yet menstruated.

D) Two divorces separated by a month.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position for divorcing a pregnant woman according to sunna is to pronounce three divorces, each separated by a month.

Divorce During Menstruation: Valid but Revocation Wajib
Ruling that divorce during menstruation is valid but revocation is obligatory according to the stronger Hanafi view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on divorce during menstruation, explain why the divorce is valid, and argue why revocation is wajib according to the stronger view.

Core Idea
Divorce during menstruation is valid but revocation is wajib to obey the Prophet's command.

This lesson examines a key ruling in Hanafi fiqh: the validity of a divorce pronounced during a wife's menstruation. Although the act is prohibited (haram) due to the timing, the divorce itself takes effect. The classical texts then discuss whether the husband must revoke it (muraja'ah) or if it is merely recommended. We will explore the evidence and the intra-madhhab debate that leads to the stronger view that revocation is obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its initial ruling
The act is talaq (divorce) during hayd. The text states it falls (waqa'a), i.e., valid. The prohibition is due to an external factor (khilaf al-awla), not because the divorce itself is invalid.
2
Locate the dalil for the ruling on revocation
The hadith: the Prophet commanded 'Umar to tell his son to revoke the divorce. The phrase 'مره فليراجعها' is a command.
3
Apply the Hanafi usul principle
In Hanafi usul, a command (amr) indicates obligation (wujub) unless there is a contrary indication. No such indication here.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Early masters interpreted the command as recommendation (mustahabb), but later authorities like Najm al-A'imma and the author of al-Hidayah said it is wajib based on the literal meaning of the amr.
The ikhtilaf is legitimate and shows the evolution of ijtihad.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The stronger view (al-ashahh) is that revocation is wajib, as adopted by the later Hanafi tradition. This is the ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا طلق الرجل امرأته في حال الحيض: وقع الطلاق. ويُستحب له أن يراجعها، (وإذا طلق الرجل امرأته في حال الحيض: وقع الطلاق)؛ لأن النهي عنه لمعنى في غيره، فلا تَنْعدم مشروعيته، (و) لكن (يُستحب له أن يراجعها). بعض قال نجم الأئمة في «الشرح»: استحباب المراجعة قولُ المشايخ، والأصح أنه واجب عملاً بحقيقة الأمر، ورفعاً للمعصية بالقدر الممكن، ومثله في «الهداية». (۱) وهو قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم لعمر بن الخطاب رضي الله عنه حين طلق ابنه عبد الله امرأته وهي حائض ، فقال له : «مره فليراجعها»، صحيح البخاري ٣٤٥/٩ (٥٢٥١)، صحيح مسلم ۱۰۹۳/۲ (١٤۷۱) ، ومُطلق الأمر يدل على الوجوب البناية .١٩/٥
(And if a man divorces his wife during her menstruation: the divorce takes effect) because the prohibition is due to an external meaning, so its legitimacy is not negated. (And) but (it is recommended for him to revoke her). Some said, Najm al-A'imma in al-Sharh: The recommendation of revocation is the statement of the early masters, and the correct view is that it is obligatory, acting upon the literal meaning of the command, and removing the disobedience as much as possible. And similar is in al-Hidayah. (1) It is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him) to 'Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with him) when his son 'Abd Allah divorced his wife while she was menstruating: 'Command him to revoke her.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, Sahih Muslim). And a general command indicates obligation.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage addresses the validity of a divorce pronounced during a woman's menstruation. The matn states that the divorce takes effect (waqa'a al-talaq) because the prohibition against it is due to an external reason (the confusion of lineage or 'iddah), not because the divorce itself is impermissible. Therefore, the divorce is valid (nafidh). The sharh then discusses whether revoking the divorce (muraja'ah) is recommended (mustahabb) or obligatory (wajib). The early masters (mashayikh) said it is mustahabb, but Najm al-A'imma and the author of al-Hidayah hold that it is wajib, based on the hadith where the Prophet commanded 'Umar to tell his son to revoke the divorce. In Hanafi usul, a command (amr) indicates obligation. The stronger view is that revocation is obligatory, as it removes the sin of the prohibited divorce. Thus, while the divorce is valid, the husband must revoke it to comply with the prophetic command.

Key Terms
الحيض (al-hayd): The menstrual period during which divorce is prohibited but valid if uttered.
المراجعة (al-muraja'ah): The act of revoking a revocable (raj'i) divorce by taking the wife back within the 'iddah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the stronger view in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on revoking a divorce pronounced during menstruation?
A) It is recommended (mustahabb).
B) It is obligatory (wajib).
C) It is prohibited (haram).
D) It is not required.

Key Takeaway
Divorce during menstruation is valid (sahih) but the husband must revoke it (wajib) based on the prophetic command and the Hanafi usul principle that a command indicates obligation.

Divorce During Menstruation: Validity, Taking Her Back, and Timing
Ruling with proof and intra-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why divorce during menstruation is valid, state the evidence for taking her back, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the permissible time for a subsequent divorce.

Core Idea
A prohibited divorce is still valid; the command to take her back is obligatory, and the timing of a second divorce is disputed between Abu Hanifa and his students.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi fiqh issue: the validity and consequences of divorcing a wife during her menstruation. While the act is prohibited, the divorce itself counts. The husband is commanded to take her back, and scholars debate whether this is recommended or obligatory. Additionally, after reconciliation, when may he divorce her again? Abu Hanifa and his two students differ, with the relied-upon position being that he must wait until after a second menstrual period.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling on divorce during hayd
Identify that the divorce is valid (sahih) even though the act is prohibited. The prohibition is for a reason external to the divorce itself, so the essence of the divorce is unaffected.
This distinguishes between the validity of the act and its prohibition.
2
Analyze the hadith and the command to take her back
The Prophet ﷺ ordered 'Umar: 'Order him to take her back.' In Hanafi usul, a command (amr) indicates obligation (wujub). Hence, taking her back is obligatory according to the stronger view.
The dalil is from Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Recognize the ikhtilaf on recommendation vs. obligation
Most mashayikh say it is mustahab (recommended), but Najm al-A'imma and al-Hidayah consider it wajib (obligatory) based on the imperative.
The mufta bihi is the obligatory view.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of subsequent divorce
After taking her back, when may the husband divorce her again? Abu Hanifa allows it in the purity following the first menstruation; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require waiting until after a second menstruation and purity.
Al-Karkhi attributes each view to the respective imams.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of the Sahibayn (wait for a second period), as it is the Zahir al-Riwayah recorded in al-Asl.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

He said in 'al-Hidayah': Thus it is mentioned in 'al-Asl', and al-Tahawi mentioned that he divorces her in the purity that follows the menstruation. Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi said: What al-Tahawi mentioned is the saying of Abu Hanifa, and what is mentioned in al-Asl is their saying (i.e. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). End. And in 'al-Tashih': al-Karkhi said: This (1) is their saying, and the saying of Abu Hanifa is that he may divorce her in the purity that follows the menstruation in which he divorced her and took her back. And he said in 'al-Kafi': What is mentioned in the book (2) is the zahir al-riwayah from (1) i.e. when she becomes pure from the menstruation in which he divorced her, then she menstruates another menstruation, and becomes pure from it, then he is given a choice... (2) i.e. Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Quduri addresses two issues related to divorce during menstruation. First, it affirms that if a man divorces his wife while she is in her menses, the divorce is valid (waqa'a al-talaq). The prohibition against such divorce (found in the hadith) is not for the act itself but for a reason external to the divorce, namely that it lengthens the 'iddah unnecessarily. Therefore the divorce is not invalid. However, the husband is recommended (yustahab) to take her back (muraja'a). The commentary notes that Najm al-A'imma reports a stronger view: it is actually obligatory (wajib) to take her back, based on the imperative form of the Prophet's command to 'Umar: 'Order him to take her back.' A general command (amr mutlaq) linguistically indicates obligation (wujub). This position is also mentioned in al-Hidayah. After taking her back, the passage then discusses the husband's subsequent options. According to the 'Asl' (i.e., the Zahir al-Riwayah of Imam Muhammad), after the wife becomes pure from that first menstruation and then menstruates again and becomes pure from that second menstruation, the husband is given a choice: he may divorce her or keep her. Al-Tahawi transmitted that Abu Hanifa held a different view: the husband may divorce her in the purity (tuhr) immediately following the first menstruation (i.e., after she becomes pure from the hayd in which he divorced her and after he has taken her back). Al-Karkhi clarifies that the ruling in al-Asl is the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), while Abu Hanifa's view is as al-Tahawi reported. The relied-upon position is from the Sahibayn as found in the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
الطلاق (al-talaq): Divorce; the dissolution of marriage by the husband's pronouncement.
الحيض (al-hayd): Menstruation; the monthly period during which a woman is impure and cannot pray or fast.
المراجعة (al-muraja'a): Taking back the wife during the 'iddah after a revocable divorce.
الأصل (al-Asl): One of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, containing the authoritative rulings of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Only after the 'iddah is complete.

Key Takeaway
Divorce during menstruation is valid; the husband must take her back (wajib); and the mufta bihi requires waiting until after a second menstruation to divorce again.

Timing of Divorce After Menstrual Period: Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of divorce after menstrual periods

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the timing of divorce after reconciliation during menstruation, and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Divorce timing after reconciliation: Abu Hanifa allows it in the first purity; Sahibayn require a second cycle.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the proper moment for a husband to divorce his wife after having reconciled with her during her menstrual period. The differing views of Abu Hanifa and his two leading disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, are examined, along with the resolution provided by later Hanafi authorities. By understanding this ikhtilaf, you will appreciate how the Hanafi school internally resolves differences among its founding imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
Read the matn portion: 'When she becomes pure, menstruates, and becomes pure, he has a choice...' This sets the default position: the husband must wait until after a second menses and subsequent purity.
This is the ruling attributed to the Sahibayn in al-Asl.
2
Locate the dispute
Notice that al-Tahawi reports an alternative: the husband may divorce in the purity that follows the menses. This is attributed to Abu Hanifa by al-Karkhi.
The dispute is over the timing: first purity vs. second purity.
3
Understand the attribution
Al-Karkhi clarifies: what is in al-Asl (requiring a second menses) is the statement of the Sahibayn; what al-Tahawi narrated is Abu Hanifa's view.
Thus both views are authentically Hanafi.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The text from al-Kafi states that the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) from Abu Hanifa is that he may divorce in the first purity. This becomes the relied-upon position.
Later authorities preferred Abu Hanifa's view as the operative ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق
فإذا طهرت، وحاضت، وطَهرت، فهو مخيّر : إن شاء طلقها، وإن شاء أمسكها . وقال برهان الأئمة المحبوبي وتجب رجعتها في الأصح. كذا في «التصحيح».
فإذا طهرت من حيضها الذي طلقها، وراجعها فيه، (وحاضت) حيضاً آخر، وطهرت) منه، (فهو): أي الزوج (مخيّر: إن شاء طلقها) ثانياً، (وإن شاء أمسكها). قال في «الهداية»: وهكذا ذُكر في «الأصل»، وذكر الطحاوي: أنه يطلقها في الطهر الذي يلي الحيضة. قال أبو الحسن الكرخي : ما ذكره الطحاوي قول أبي حنيفة، وما ذكر في الأصل قولهما. اهـ وفي «التصحيح»: قال الكرخي : هذا قولهما، وقولُ أبي حنيفة: له أن يطلقها في الطهر الذي يلي الحيضة التي طلقها، وراجعها فيه. وقال في الكافي»: المذكور في الكتاب : ظاهر الرواية عن أبي حنيفة)، والذي ذكره الكرخي رواية عن أبي حنيفة. اهـ
Book of Divorce. When she becomes pure, menstruates, and becomes pure, he has a choice: if he wishes he divorces her, and if he wishes he keeps her. Burhan al-A'imma al-Mahbubi said: and her return (to him) is obligatory in the most correct view. Likewise in al-Tashih. When she becomes pure from her menses in which he divorced her and reconciled with her, and (she menstruates) another menses, and (becomes pure) from it, (then he): meaning the husband (has a choice: if he wishes he divorces her) a second time, (and if he wishes he keeps her). He said in al-Hidaya: likewise it is mentioned in al-Asl, and al-Tahawi mentioned that he divorces her in the purity that follows the menses. Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi said: what al-Tahawi mentioned is the statement of Abu Hanifa, and what is mentioned in al-Asl is their statement (i.e., of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). End. And in al-Tashih: al-Karkhi said: this is their statement, and the statement of Abu Hanifa: he has the right to divorce her in the purity that follows the menses in which he divorced her and reconciled with her. And it is said in al-Kafi: what is mentioned in the book (al-Quduri) is the apparent narration from Abu Hanifa, and what al-Karkhi mentioned is a narration from Abu Hanifa. End.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the proper timing for a husband to divorce his wife after having reconciled with her during her menstrual period. The base ruling (from Quduri's matn) states that if a husband divorces his wife during her menses, he must wait until she completes that menses and then has another menses and then becomes pure again; at that point he may either divorce her or keep her. However, there is a difference of opinion among the early Hanafi scholars. According to Imam al-Tahawi's narration, Abu Hanifa held that the husband may divorce her in the first period of purity (tahr) after the menses in which he divorced her and reconciled. In contrast, the 'Original' (al-Asl) — representing the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (al-Sahibayn) — requires waiting until after a second menses and subsequent purity. Al-Karkhi clarifies that the view in al-Asl is that of the two disciples, while al-Tahawi's narration reflects Abu Hanifa's position. The text from al-Tashih confirms this and then notes that the view cited in al-Kafi (i.e., the later compendium) states that the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) from Abu Hanifa is that he may divorce immediately after the first purity, while al-Karkhi's reported view is a rare (nawadir) transmission. In practice, the mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is the one attributed to Abu Hanifa in the apparent narration, but the student should be aware of this internal ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
الطهر (al-tuhr): The state of purity from menstruation; in this context, the period after menstrual bleeding has ceased.
الرجعية (al-raj'iyya): Reversible divorce; the wife remains in marriage during the 'iddah and the husband may take her back without a new contract.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwaya): The well-known, widely transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad's six books (the zahir al-riwayah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Abu Hanifa
B) Sahibayn
C) Al-Tahawi
D) Al-Karkhi

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position allows divorce in the first purity after reconciliation, not requiring a second menstrual cycle.

Validity of Divorce: Only from an Adult, Sane Husband
Ruling on whose divorce is valid: conditions and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid divorce and identify which persons' divorce is valid or invalid according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Divorce is valid only from an adult sane husband; compulsion and drunkenness do not invalidate.

Divorce is a serious legal act with strict conditions. This passage from al-Quduri clarifies whose divorce counts: only a husband who is both adult and sane. It then addresses tricky cases – compulsion, drunkenness, minority, and insanity – explaining when the divorce takes effect and when it does not. Understanding these rules protects the legal status of marriages and prevents mistakes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The passage states that divorce is valid from every husband who is baligh (adult) and 'aqil (sane). These are the essential conditions.
Adulthood and sanity are prerequisites for legal capacity (ahliyyat al-ada').
2
Note the exceptions that are included
Even if the husband is compelled (mukrah) or drunk from a prohibited substance (sakran bi-mahzur), his divorce is still valid. The Hanafi school considers the utterance intentional in both cases.
For the drunk, validity is a penalty; for the compelled, it is because he chose the lesser harm.
3
Identify the invalid cases
The divorce of a minor (sabi) and an insane person (majnoon) is invalid regardless of circumstances, except for a specific conditional case for the insane.
A minor's divorce is invalid even if he later becomes adult and confirms it.
4
Analyze the sub-rules for the invalid cases
For the minor: if after adulthood he says 'I divorced her' using the past tense, it counts as a new divorce. For the insane: his divorce is invalid unless he made a conditional divorce (ta'liq) while sane, then became insane, and the condition occurs.
This exception preserves the original intent made during sanity.
5
Understand the rationale
Compulsion and drunkenness do not remove legal capacity entirely; the utterance is still considered voluntary. Minority and insanity remove capacity, so no legal effect attaches.
The distinction is based on the presence of choice and understanding at the time of utterance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان من يقع طلاقهم، ومن لا يقع :
(ويقع طلاق كل زوج إذا كان بالغاً عاقلاً) ولو مكرهاً(2)، أو سكران بمحظور.
* (ولا يقع طلاق الصبي) ولو مراهقاً، أو أجازه بعد البلوغ. أما لو قال : أوقعته : وقع؛ لأنه ابتداء إيقاع.
(و) لا طلاق (المجنون)، إلا إذا علَّق عاقلاً، ثم جُنَّ، فوجد الشرط (3).
Statement of those whose divorce is valid and those whose divorce is not valid: (The divorce of every husband is valid if he is an adult, sane) even if compelled, or drunk due to a prohibited (substance). (And the divorce of a minor is not valid) even if approaching puberty, or if he authorizes it after puberty. But if he says: 'I pronounce [it]', it is valid; because it is an initiation of effect. (And) no divorce (of the insane), except if he suspended (the divorce) while sane, then became insane, and the condition occurs.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from al-Quduri's matn, parsed and explained by the commentator. It establishes the conditions for a valid divorce. The key conditions are that the husband must be an adult (baligh) and sane ('aqil). The divorce of anyone who lacks these conditions is invalid. The passage then addresses exceptions: (1) If a husband is forced (mukrah) to pronounce divorce, his divorce is still valid because he intentionally uttered the words; he is not excused because he chose the lesser harm. (2) If he is drunk due to a prohibited substance (i.e., intentionally consuming something haram), his divorce is also valid as a penalty. For a minor (sabi), even if he is baligh by puberty (murahiq) or later confirms the divorce after reaching adulthood, the divorce does not take effect. However, if after adulthood he says 'I divorced (such-and-such)' using the past tense (awqa'tu), then it counts as a new divorce initiated at that moment. For an insane person (majnoon), his divorce is invalid, except if he made a conditional divorce (ta'liq) while sane and then became insane; if the condition occurs during his insanity, the divorce takes effect. This is because the original intent was made when he was legally responsible.

Key Terms
البالغ (al-baligh): A person who has reached puberty, legally an adult.
العاقل (al-'aqil): A person of sound mind; sane.
المكرَه (al-mukrah): One who is compelled under threat to utter divorce.
السكران بمحظور (al-sakran bi-mahzur): One who is intoxicated by a prohibited substance (e.g., wine, drugs) intentionally.
الصبي (al-sabi): A male child who has not reached puberty.
المجنون (al-majnoon): An insane person; one lacking sanity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is the divorce of an insane person valid according to this passage?
A) It is never valid.
B) It is valid if the insane person was sane at the time of marriage.
C) It is valid if the condition for divorce was made while he was sane and the condition occurs after he becomes insane.
D) It is valid if he later becomes sane and confirms the divorce.

Key Takeaway
A valid divorce requires the husband to be an adult and sane at the time of utterance; compulsion and drunkenness from haram do not invalidate, but minority and insanity do.
